  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d24c9e12-e3f4-49a9-acab-c42669ad1e1b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

In strange other worlds, Lionheart must face a lyrical yet lethal tiger, a fallen unicorn, and a goblin horde on his quest to rescue the girl he betrayed. <br /><br />With the Night of Moonblood fast approaching--when King Vahe seeks to wake the Dragon's sleeping children--Lionheart must discover whether or not his heart contains courage before it's too late for Rose Red...and all those he loves.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1627244-hey-guys-curious-reader-here-so-do-we">Hey guys! curious reader here. So, do we ever hear anything about Princess and Prince Aethelbald again in the series (other than Heartless)?. Honestly, I&#39;d be genuinely disappointed if that wasn&#39;t the case; I kind of grew to like them.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/60442394-hannah-sorenson"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1593117249i/60442394._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/60442394-hannah-sorenson">Hannah Sorenson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">At this point, I'm sure you've already read more of the series, but I'll answer the question anyway. I've only read the first three of the series, but<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">At this point, I'm sure you've already read more of the series, but I'll answer the question anyway. I've only read the first three of the series, but we do see some mentions about Princess Una and Prince Aethelbald. Although I haven't read anything in their POV, I still learned some new things about them. Prince Aethelbald is mentioned a lot throughout the three books I've read. Keep in mind that they aren't the main characters, so they aren't the focus of the book. Hope this helps you!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16872008510533206035">March 2019:<br/><br/>This is actually my fourth time reading this one? And wow, it’s so good to revisit this story. I remembered nearly everything, but this story...my goodness, it’s like coming home. My sweet, sweet babies. *hugs them allllll* *except Vahe he totally deserves what he got* <br/><br/>UPDATE FOR JULY '17 REREAD: <br/>It's still so beautiful and I will never get over it. It didn't lose anything on the second read (except that I knew a couple of the plot twists.) <br/><br/>Shrieky fangirly review: [insert here]<br/><br/>Okay, </span>
  <span id="freeText16872008510533206035" style="display:none">March 2019:<br /><br />This is actually my fourth time reading this one? And wow, it’s so good to revisit this story. I remembered nearly everything, but this story...my goodness, it’s like coming home. My sweet, sweet babies. *hugs them allllll* *except Vahe he totally deserves what he got* <br /><br />UPDATE FOR JULY '17 REREAD: <br />It's still so beautiful and I will never get over it. It didn't lose anything on the second read (except that I knew a couple of the plot twists.) <br /><br />Shrieky fangirly review: [insert here]<br /><br />Okay, I'm out now. *drops mic*<br /><br />MAY '17 ORIGINAL REVIEW<br /><br />My feels are crushed.<br /><br />My ships are sinking.<br /><br />My heart is broken.<br /><br />And yet this is one of the best books of the year.<br /><br />The books have gotten progressively better, too. Heartless was good but not great, Veiled Rose was better, and now Moonblood is the best thing EVER. This means Starflower must be the best book in history. XD<br /><br />Some things I loved: <br />-Everything<br />-Rose Red/ Varvare. She's one of my all time favorite characters now. <br />-Leo. He just gets better with every book. I despised him in the first one, tolerated him in the second, and now... *huggles Leo* Ooohhhh, I love this author.<br />-I adore Ragniprava and Vahe and Anahid as villains too.<br />-The unicorn was kind of amazing too. I hated it... and then loved it... I think I ended up loving it?<br />-And Eanrin. Oh my word. I love him so much . He is my favorite. I can't wait for Starflower. He's like the main character in that one.<br />-Imraldera and Oeric and King Iubdan and Felix and... the characters are the best.<br />-The Night of Moonblood. Stengl has a way of befuddling me so that I have no idea what the plot twists will be? And it's kind of amazing?<br /><br />What I didn't like:<br />-that one plot twist? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Where Leo died? But then didn't? And that's nothing wrong with that, just my feels... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />-The fact that my ships are sinking? And I think Stengl isn't writing any more Goldstone Wood books, which means... I'll never find out if my ship is going to work. *sobs*<br /><br />Finally: Read it. Please. Read the other ones too, but please, read them. You won't regret it.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211162664" />
    <a title="E.F.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b"><img alt="E.F.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424876183p2/39244832.jpg" /></a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes YA fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=books-i-ll-read-again">books-i-ll-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=made-me-cry-in-a-good-way">made-me-cry-in-a-good-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=made-me-smile">made-me-smile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211162664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13750107773415997848">Updated review: "We bless the name of he who sits Enthroned beyond the Highlands.<br/>We bless his name and sing in answer<br/>To the song he gave." -The Night of Moonblood poem, page 244.<br/><br/>Having now read this book for a second time, my positive opinion of it still stands. The themes of redemption, forgiveness, unconditional love, true beauty, and keeping faith even when it's difficult, all shine through as brilliantly as Hymlume's children sparkling in the night sky. And yes, I did cry multiple times AGAI</span>
  <span id="freeText13750107773415997848" style="display:none">Updated review: "We bless the name of he who sits Enthroned beyond the Highlands.<br>We bless his name and sing in answer<br>To the song he gave." -The Night of Moonblood poem, page 244.<br><br>Having now read this book for a second time, my positive opinion of it still stands. The themes of redemption, forgiveness, unconditional love, true beauty, and keeping faith even when it's difficult, all shine through as brilliantly as Hymlume's children sparkling in the night sky. And yes, I did cry multiple times AGAIN, even though I knew what happens!<br><br>Actual footage of me re-reading the end of the story:

              <span id="reviewTextContainer301090972" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8211497826656691800">Don't you love it when you find that book(or series) that you absolutely feel the need to gush about?! I definitely feel the need to gush about The Tales of Goldstone Wood series. My first instinct is to say that Moonblood has been my favorite book so far. In actuality, all the books are sort of one long story, though. (There's never been a huge cliffhanger, which I greatly appreciate). As much as I've loved the series after reading the first two books, it's with the addition of Moonblood that m</span>
  <span id="freeText8211497826656691800" style="display:none">Don't you love it when you find that book(or series) that you absolutely feel the need to gush about?! I definitely feel the need to gush about The Tales of Goldstone Wood series. My first instinct is to say that Moonblood has been my favorite book so far. In actuality, all the books are sort of one long story, though. (There's never been a huge cliffhanger, which I greatly appreciate). As much as I've loved the series after reading the first two books, it's with the addition of Moonblood that my opinion of the series has been drastically raised. I can easily see this series achieving Classic status. It has became one of my all-time favorite series EVER, and I can't wait to re-read each of these books to discover more of the hidden meanings. As all the little details and characters keep coming together, I can see the brilliance of the story. Once again, I HIGHLY recommend you read these in publication order.<br /><br />Amazingly, I'm even more excited about Starflower, because it appears it will go back in time for us to read Eanrin's background story. As much as I adore most of the characters in this series, Eanrin is by far my favorite, despite his arrogant nature. I simply adore Eanrin's character! In Heartless, he only had a somewhat small part, and I don't recall him being in Veiled Rose at all. In Moonblood, we really get to know him better. Lord willing, I'm thankful I only have to wait until October, instead of a whole year to pick it up, which would break my heart!<br /><br />I do want to point out that The Goldstone Wood Series is definitely Christian in nature, but it can be read completely separate from Christian thoughts if that is what you'd prefer. I'd say if you really and truly like The Chronicles of Narnia, The Goldstone Series should be right up your alley.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9484435319375029842">Oh my goodness, what can I say about this book? I guess we will start off with this:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380431191ra/865112.gif' width='245px' height='245px' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Anne Elisabeth Stengl is a phenomenal author. Her books have such an extremely intricate plot, and it's amazing how she weaves everything together.<br/>There were so many times that I felt like throwing the book at the wall. This is because of how masterfully imperfect the characters are- seriously they defy <i>all</i> stereotypes. As vexing as it was, all the flaws and mistakes made by the characters are so refreshing and r</span>
  <span id="freeText9484435319375029842" style="display:none">Oh my goodness, what can I say about this book? I guess we will start off with this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380431191ra/865112.gif" width="245px" height="245px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Anne Elisabeth Stengl is a phenomenal author. Her books have such an extremely intricate plot, and it's amazing how she weaves everything together.<br>There were so many times that I felt like throwing the book at the wall. This is because of how masterfully imperfect the characters are- seriously they defy <i>all</i> stereotypes. As vexing as it was, all the flaws and mistakes made by the characters are so refreshing and realistic! <br>For example, Lionheart being the anti-hero. I have never seen this happen, but everything about him from the ending of <i>Veiled Rose</i> throughout this book left no question to it. <br><br>Also, there is Rose Red who <b>is the most sweet and heartbreaking character ever,</b> but nothing ever goes right for her.<br>I am so tired of every main character I read being breathtakingly beautiful and not knowing it- Rose Red shatters that stereotype with her goblin face and all her veils. All of the anguish she suffered because of her looks was agonizing, but sent such a wonderful message because of her personality. She makes a good contrast to Lionheart.<br><br>And then, of course, there is Eanrin. His wit is so alluring. I started reading his banter and immediately was like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384993764ra/7041294.gif" width="500px" height="246px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously, Eanrin is amazing. And strangely, he is even more enticing because he is blind.<br><br>This book had so many positive messages. The symbolism and tones were all very powerful and intriguingly placed. A well deserved 5 stars!<br></span>

  <span id="freeText9100727720268127937" style="display:none">I don't feel like writing an actual review, BUT I did kind of spill all my thoughts in the readalong thread when I read this, so I may as well just post that here as my review! <br /><br /><b>In brief:</b><br /><br />I LOVE THIS BOOK SO SO MUCH AND IT'S MY FAVE GOLDSTONE WOOD YET AND I'M ADDICTED AND IT'S SO FAE AND PERILOUS AND BEAUTIFUL AND WELL-WRITTEN AND WHY DID IT TAKE SO LONG FOR ME TO READ IT?? <br /><br />Also Oeric. XD Am I the only one who loves how he covers up all sorts of deeper darker sadder emotions with his bright smile? AWK. And then he was Vahe's TWIN BROTHER AND JUST!!!! *flailing around* That whole plot was so so awesome!!! And I love how he and Beana are a thing, and how that ties in with Rose Red, and Vahe, and and and ALL THE THINGS. So. much. epic. Oeric is like one of my favorites too. :D (And he and Beana are so cute halp.)<br /><br />Of course I love Leo and Rosie, even when they're stubborn idiots, but I love them anyway. ^_^ Their story is SO SWEET. &lt;3 And I love that Leo did end up going on a quest to find her. He's not ALL bad. ;) Also, at the end when it was saying that certain poets would be furious at them, I was imagining Eanrin eavesdropping on them. XD Buuut if he actually was, I suspect he might have jumped out and done something about it, so... maybe not.<br /><br />Poor empty-headed Felix a.k.a. the Boy was SO SAD. O_O But he's okay now and I'M SO RELIEVED. &lt;3 I do really like Felix. :) Although I was sliiiightly disappointed he was the one to kill the Bane of Corrilond instead of Leo--partly because I was reading that whole ending part WAY TOO FAST and accidentally read it wrong where I thought "he" who was fighting the dragon WAS Leo, not Felix, so... yeah. Oops. But yay for the Prince and fixing things and yes. ^_^<br /><br />I absolutely LOVE Leo and Eanrin having to travel around together and their bickering and stuff and how they don't get along. IT'S THE BEST. &lt;3 Of course they would end up with each other when they dislike each other so much. XD And them traveling through Faerie etc. and the Wood Between was SO AWESOME! Ragniprava, too. XD<br /><br />The unicorn is terrifying and heartbreaking but YES at the end and just ALL THE MEEP. O_O<br /><br />Also, everything about Anahid and about Diarmid and about both of them is HEARTBREAKING. STAHP. D: Ahem.<br /><br />Vahe is INSANE and creepy and No. O_O He was actually a fascinating villain to read about. XD<br /><br />But... the picture of the Gold Stone etc.... It's the Dragon and Oeric and Vahe and who's the third lookalike?? And... Beana?? :O I'M SO CURIOUS. Do we get the story of that in Golden Daughter or... not? XD (I mean, you don't have to answer that because spoilers, but. Anyway...) Also, all the "Night of Moonblood" stuff, with the poem and the legend and all of it was SOOO AMAZING AND EPIC AND TRAGIC AND EMOTIONAL! EEP.<br /><br />One of my favorite things, besides the awesome characters I love, is how absolutely GORGEOUS and PERILOUS and FAE this book is! Just... I'm blown away by the incredible writing and the Faerie-ness and all the peril but beauty and just otherworldliness. It's SO amazingly done! &lt;3 And the plot and characters and everything are just interwoven so brilliantly, with everything just working out in these oh-so-fitting ways, and I don't even know how to explain it, but this story of traveling in different Fae worlds and the prince and the goblin princess and the various star-crossed love stories around with Eanrin and Imraldera and Oeric and Beana and Anahid and Diarmid and all the intrigue and subplots and just the sheer EPICNESS of these interweaving plots and how they feel RIGHT and steeped in deepness and rich tapestries of story. And I can't even explain it, but THIS BOOK IS JUST SO GOOD AND I LOVE IT!! Sorry if that was vague. XD<br /><br />So. There are some thoughts from me as the "new" reader of Goldstone Wood for these readalongs. XD But I'm totally hooked now on this series and I love it. ^_^ Moonblood is definitely my favorite so far! :D <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="9100727720268127937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9062601638497103793">Beautiful. That's Moonblood in one word. Beautiful. So fantastic and merry and full of vibrant, rich color, while at the same time, mysterious, mythical and solemn. It truly holds the meaning of Fantasy. <br/><br/>Stengl has a hilarious way of writing that just kept me smiling, and sometimes laughing. But at the same time the story is perfectly serious and more believable and real than the pages I kept turning so quickly.<br/><br/>It is also epic. Moonblood is a sweeping epic adventure, filled with mystery, magic a</span>
  <span id="freeText9062601638497103793" style="display:none">Beautiful. That's Moonblood in one word. Beautiful. So fantastic and merry and full of vibrant, rich color, while at the same time, mysterious, mythical and solemn. It truly holds the meaning of Fantasy. <br /><br />Stengl has a hilarious way of writing that just kept me smiling, and sometimes laughing. But at the same time the story is perfectly serious and more believable and real than the pages I kept turning so quickly.<br /><br />It is also epic. Moonblood is a sweeping epic adventure, filled with mystery, magic and marvelous characters.<br /><br />Just how many books can be epic, hilarious and beautiful at the same time?<br /><br />It is also one of THE greatest works Christian Fiction ever written. A more inspiring novel would be hard to find. Inspiring, moving and uplifting, Moonblood currently takes the place of best Christian book I've ever read, save one.<br /><br />The characters were also great. I love Lionheart. Rose Red is extremely likeable. The new characters were all great too. Eanrin was just fantastic. And it was so fun to see Felix again.<br />The worlds were just amazing. Faerie is so otherworldy, beautiful but dangerous.<br /><br />Moonblood is practically perfect.<br /><br /><b>EDIT</b> after first re-read: I'm leaving the below complaint because it was part of my original review, but it is no longer valid. Because of the comments way down there, and the fact that I just re-read it and it felt better I now don't mind and think the ending is wonderful! It IS still a bit sad, but it's a beautiful sad.<br />[[Unfortunately no book is really perfect. The ending was not exactly Happily Ever After. Though I felt it was fitting and how it really happened, I was not satisfied. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I felt that after two whole books with Lionheart and Rose Red they should have a happily ever after. Though the ending left room for them to get together again someday it isn't certain and they didn't even say they loved each other! I might not be complaining if I knew there would be more books with them, but for all I know, their story is over in the sense that we won't see them again in future books. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So if you only read books that end 100 percent happily then Moonblood isn't for you. It's only 90 percent happy.]]<br /><br />But I can't win every time, and for once I will accept a slightly sad ending. (This is world shattering news by the way.)<br /><br />With characters, worlds and a story you will never forget, Anne Elisabeth Stengl's third Tale of Goldstone Wood will appeal to readers of all genres and ages.</span>

        <a title="m a r y l i z" class="user" itemprop="url" name="m a r y l i z" href="/user/show/56772107-m-a-r-y-l-i-z">m a r y l i z</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5179756997842147413">Well, that may have been the most painful book I've read in a while.<br/><br/>It took me nearly two weeks--<i>two weeks</i>--to read this book. Normally, I finish a book in about 2 to 4 days soooo...yeah. That says a lot about how interested I was in this. :P<br/><br/>I still can't quite figure out what it is about the series that isn't clicking with me. Because with every successive book in the series, my interest wanes and my desire to read the book diminishes. The writing is gorgeous, the allegory exquisitely done, and</span>
  <span id="freeText5179756997842147413" style="display:none">Well, that may have been the most painful book I've read in a while.<br /><br />It took me nearly two weeks--<i>two weeks</i>--to read this book. Normally, I finish a book in about 2 to 4 days soooo...yeah. That says a lot about how interested I was in this. :P<br /><br />I still can't quite figure out what it is about the series that isn't clicking with me. Because with every successive book in the series, my interest wanes and my desire to read the book diminishes. The writing is gorgeous, the allegory exquisitely done, and the worldbuilding a masterpiece--SO WHY THE HECK DON'T I LIKE IT??<br /><br />I honestly don't know. I don't have an answer. But for some unbeknownst reason, I dreaded reading this book more than any book I can remember.<br /><br />Now, I will say there are a few things I loved about Moonblood...<br /><br />1. Eanrin + Imraldera (The best part of the book, by far)<br />2. The Tiger scenes (don't ask me why--I guess they just reminded me of the Jungle Book, but they were really cool *nods*)<br />3. The last 50 pages (they were just gahhhhhh the most beautiful thing ever &lt;3333 I LOVED HOW IT FINISHED)<br /><br />So all this to say, the fault does not lie with the author. (Because gosh, this author is <i>skilled</i>.) This series just doesn't click with me, and for that, I'm deeply saddened. I had hoped to enjoy it, and so far, that has not been the case. :( <br /><br />2.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_726969384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/726969384" />
    <a title="H.S.J. Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24203261-h-s-j-williams"><img alt="H.S.J. Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529192778p2/24203261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/726969384?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H.S.J. Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="H.S.J. Williams" href="/user/show/24203261-h-s-j-williams">H.S.J. Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24203261-h-s-j-williams?shelf=brilliance">brilliance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24203261-h-s-j-williams?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24203261-h-s-j-williams?shelf=awesome-heroes">awesome-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24203261-h-s-j-williams?shelf=reviews-five-star">reviews-five-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer726969384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6834710484196352507">When I first heard of "Heartless," I was intrigued by the front cover, and semi-interested by the summary. Eventually, I obtained a copy from a library and read it in one day. I was amazed by the complexity and beauty of the book, which had nearly moved me to tears. I was ecstatic when I discovered that more books were coming out and soon received the next two, "Veiled Rose" and "Moonblood."<br/><br/>"Veiled Rose," though good, did not pull me in as much as the first, but nevertheless I was thrilled to me</span>
  <span id="freeText6834710484196352507" style="display:none">When I first heard of "Heartless," I was intrigued by the front cover, and semi-interested by the summary. Eventually, I obtained a copy from a library and read it in one day. I was amazed by the complexity and beauty of the book, which had nearly moved me to tears. I was ecstatic when I discovered that more books were coming out and soon received the next two, "Veiled Rose" and "Moonblood."<br /><br />"Veiled Rose," though good, did not pull me in as much as the first, but nevertheless I was thrilled to meet the maiden Rose Red, and learn the story of Lionheart, whom I felt sorry for in Heartless.<br /><br />Then I read "Moonblood," which soon picks up after the end of "Heartless." This story grabbed me like few have.<br /><br />I'm an avid reader, and I have read MANY books, both well-known and unknown. But after a few days of reflection, I decided that "Tales of Goldstone Wood" was my favorite fantasy series of all time! (Topping even the Lord of the Rings books for enjoyment anyway.) I had to share them, so I read them to my mother. She loved them, though at first concerned that they dwelt on darkness. (It didn't.) She felt a lot of understanding for Una, as she had gone through a nightmare herself as a young woman before being rescued by Jesus Christ.<br /><br />"Moonblood" is a story of love, grace, forgiveness, and redemption. The main character, Lionheart, wants to be a good guy, but he's a people pleaser, and the people hate his best friend, the mysterious veiled girl, Rose Red, who terrifies the kingdom of Southlands. Afraid of losing his kingdom, Lionheart reluctantly banishes her to the dreaded Wilderlands. Soon afterwards, the rest of Lionheart's life falls to shambles. It is then that the second part of the book returns to a familiar character: Prince Felix, whose condition of dragon poisoning is becoming worse and worse. It his story that leads us to the land of Arpiar, a place of artificial beauty, overseen by the divinely beautiful King Vahe, and guarded by the evil, but haunted, unicorn. It is in Arpiar, the land of the Veiled Folk, that we are reunited with Rose Red, who has hardened her heart against the Prince of Farthestshore and Lionheart. Meanwhile, Lionheart bumbles his way through adventures with an unlikely guide: the cat Monster, otherwise known as Eanrin. (Or "sir," or "Your Grace", or "Your Eminence.") Eanrin likes Lionheart little, and Lionheart hates cats, so the two get on each others nerves in a hilarious way, especially when Lionheart learns Eanrin's secret. In this book we also re-meet, Lady Imraldera, who has a fascinating past strongly intertwined with Eanrin's. And we re-meet Sir Oreic, the ugly but noble knight, with a dark past that traces right back to Arpiar.<br />The author weaves all of these stories and more into a tapestry of adventure, beauty, and truth. The story draws to a pulse-pounding climax in which Lionheart attempts to earn absolution for his sins. But there is none who can redeem save the Prince of the land called Farthestshore...<br /><br />I'm dying for the prequel covering Imraldera and Eanrin's past, "Starflower" and the book after that "Dragonwitch."<br />Please read these books with an ready-to-learn mind, because if you resent Una and Lionheart, you might be more like them then you want to admit.<br /><br />Congratulations to Anne Elizabeth Stengel! She is an author blessed with the chance to change lives for God's Glory!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6834710484196352507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_667702317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667702317" />
    <a title="Joy C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10371233-joy-c"><img alt="Joy C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501595922p2/10371233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6772210696718624923">I loved this book! I enjoyed it so much I made myself savor it and not rush through it in one sitting. It is a wonderful continuation of the adventure of Lionheart and Rose Red and Felix. This is book three in the series and they must be read in order. The first is Heartless and the second is Veiled Rose. If you haven't read Veiled Rose then there are a couple spoilers in this review.<br/><br/>The people and land of Southlands is slowly recovering from the dragon’s prolonged stay. Prince Lionheart was the</span>
  <span id="freeText6772210696718624923" style="display:none">I loved this book! I enjoyed it so much I made myself savor it and not rush through it in one sitting. It is a wonderful continuation of the adventure of Lionheart and Rose Red and Felix. This is book three in the series and they must be read in order. The first is Heartless and the second is Veiled Rose. If you haven't read Veiled Rose then there are a couple spoilers in this review.<br /><br />The people and land of Southlands is slowly recovering from the dragon’s prolonged stay. Prince Lionheart was the only one who did not experience those five years in the country and no one quite knows what he did. But they do know that the prince acts strange and they blame it on that mysterious veiled girl who isn’t quite a girl. Rose Red.<br /><br />When Lionheart reluctantly banishes Rose Red she disappears. Unbeknownst to him he just condemned her to capture by the evil goblin King Vahe who rules the hidden realm of Arpiar and who is also Rose Red’s father. King Vahe has spent centuries waiting, plotting and planning for the Night of Moonblood when he will gain the power to rule the whole world – both the Far and the Near World.<br /><br />Lionheart is miserable and vows to redeem himself by finding Rose Red. Little does he know what awaits him when he follows Monster (Yes! Felix and Una’s cat returns!) into the mysterious Goldstone Wood. Legends come to life, tigers turn into men, a beautiful but terrifying unicorn searches for him. Can Lionheart renounce his pride and arrogance, can he accept forgiveness, can he face his worst nightmare?<br /><br />I loved learning more about the history of Goldstone Wood (and surrounding – connected? areas). It still amazes me how Anne Elisabeth has woven such a complex tale. This book really ties the first two books together and shows just how epic of a series The Tales of Goldstone Wood can become.<br /><br />It was so cool to discover who Monster actually is. After all, a blind cat who talks can't just be a cat; he’s got to be Somebody! And what a history he has! After Aslan, I think Monster is my favorite literary cat…who isn’t just a cat.<br /><br />Lionheart’s struggle is an all too human struggle. Admitting our mistakes and bowing our knee to God. I absolutely loved the many forgiveness and redemption stories found in this novel.<br /><br />This definitely gets 5 out of 5 roses. If you enjoy fantasy, adventure, grand tales, or stories about finding oneself then you should definitely read this book.<br /><br />Review first posted on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rinasreading.blogspot.com/2012/05/moonblood-by-anne-elisabeth-stengl.html">http://rinasreading.blogspot.com/2012...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6772210696718624923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_473767617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473767617" />
    <a title="Beka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4442300-beka"><img alt="Beka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585884707p2/4442300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473767617?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beka" href="/user/show/4442300-beka">Beka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=mythology-to-die-for">mythology-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=kickbutt-heroines">kickbutt-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=christian-protag">christian-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=allegory">allegory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4442300-beka?shelf=beautiful-words">beautiful-words</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473767617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13649788241830585236"><i>Moonblood</i> is the third book in the series "The Tales of Goldstone Wood" by Anne Elisabeth Stengl. It flows directly from the ending of <i>Veiled Rose</i>, so I highly suggest you read that one first. While I enjoyed <i>Veiled Rose</i>, I absolutely adored <i>Moonblood</i>. And here's why:<br/><br/><b>1.) The characters:</b> Having read <i>Heartless</i> and <i>Veiled Rose</i>, I already had the background knowledge necessary to truly appreciate how Stengl wove the character interaction. Everyone stayed consistent while still growing. Some characte</span>
  <span id="freeText13649788241830585236" style="display:none"><i>Moonblood</i> is the third book in the series "The Tales of Goldstone Wood" by Anne Elisabeth Stengl. It flows directly from the ending of <i>Veiled Rose</i>, so I highly suggest you read that one first. While I enjoyed <i>Veiled Rose</i>, I absolutely adored <i>Moonblood</i>. And here's why:<br /><br /><b>1.) The characters:</b> Having read <i>Heartless</i> and <i>Veiled Rose</i>, I already had the background knowledge necessary to truly appreciate how Stengl wove the character interaction. Everyone stayed consistent while still growing. Some characters even backpedaled, showing sides to themselves that I wasn't sure existed. And Lionheart, despite his position as main protagonist, does not get any easy breaks, even at the end.<br /><br /><b>2.) The setting:</b> If there is one fantasy world I will never tire of learning about, it is Stengl's Goldstone Wood. Like Tolkien, she gives just enough information about the world to entice us without revealing all her secrets. Secondary characters become real and vibrant entities, ones that make you wonder about their own histories. I especially loved the Tiger, and would love to see more stories about his exploits one day.<br /><br /><b>3.) The romance:</b> It is very difficult to find romance that is pure but still has the power to break your heart. Without spoiling the book, I will simply say that sometimes fewer words says it all--and the ending, though happy, is not how bards would tell it.<br /><br /><b>4.) The writing:</b> Lyrical--breezy at times, sombre at others. The song of Hymlume and the scene interwoven throughout made me cry. The sheer beauty of it--the grief and the longing for times of innocence and true love--I honestly had to blink very rapidly to keep from weeping like a child.<br /><br /><b>5.) The themes:</b> I've heard it said that love is earned, and I think that's stupid, for reasons I will not get into. In the same way, redemption cannot be earned, because we can never atone for our sins the way we should. This book handles this idea very beautifully. I struggled along with Lionheart to accept this, and watching his struggle endeared me to his character for the first time in this series. I hated him in <i>Heartless</i>, was okay with him in <i>Veiled Rose</i>, and loved him in <i>Moonblood</i>. I hope this isn't the end of his story!<br /><br /><b>6.) Eanrin and Imraldera:</b> I can't resist. They are two of my favourite fictional characters ever. Their moments in this book are few, but completely stole the show for me. Like I said before, Stengl says a lot in few words, and I was melting like chocolate. Though Eanrin has to stop being such a cat! (And if you don't understand a word of this, it means you have to hurry up and read this series to find out!)<br /><br />I could go on and on about this book, but I have a midterm to study for and <i>Dragonwitch</i> to start pondering. Do yourself a favour and lose yourself in the series "The Tales of Goldstone Wood"!<br /><br />Five Stars!<br /><br />Find reviews and more at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thewriterofdreamthings.blogspot.com">www.thewriterofdreamthings.blogspot.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13649788241830585236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1007097908" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1007097908" />
    <a title="Michael Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6236139-michael-jones"><img alt="Michael Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382869511p2/6236139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1007097908?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Jones" href="/user/show/6236139-michael-jones">Michael Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6236139-michael-jones?shelf=honorable-romance">honorable-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6236139-michael-jones?shelf=brings-animals-to-human-intelligenc">brings-animals-to-human-intelligenc</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1007097908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9782738350542938283">Okay, I'm totally changing this to a 5 star review. I have read much more carefully this time and the depth is astounding. She draws characters both masculine and feminine with a lot of reflection on how people interact and try to live as Christians. This series in particular gives me great encouragement to run the Christian race despite my failings personally. I can't give a high enough recommendation for Christians who enjoy good fantasy fiction. And despite the slightly chick flick covers on </span>
  <span id="freeText9782738350542938283" style="display:none">Okay, I'm totally changing this to a 5 star review. I have read much more carefully this time and the depth is astounding. She draws characters both masculine and feminine with a lot of reflection on how people interact and try to live as Christians. This series in particular gives me great encouragement to run the Christian race despite my failings personally. I can't give a high enough recommendation for Christians who enjoy good fantasy fiction. And despite the slightly chick flick covers on the books, there is plenty of good down-home masculinity in this series. <br /><br />This particular book does a great job with the inner conflict and struggle that Lionheart goes through when he has to deal with compromises that he has made and loyalties he must be willing to die for.<br /><br />This is my 3rd book in the series which I have enjoyed immensely. My children have definitely fallen in love with Lionheart: he is an awesome and genuinely brave character.<br /><br />Also, I'm coming to trust the author. She leads you into deep and dark evil, but her characters maintain their integrity. She wrestles with the themes of inward beauty and outward beauty: the Princess is also a goblin, depending on which world she finds herself in.<br /><br />Lionheart has betrayed his goblin Princess, sees what an awful thing he has done, and so is willing to sacrifice himself to save her. In the process, he learns about the fairy world firsthand!<br /><br />This book is deep. Really deep., In fact, it was a little too deep for my younger children when I tried to read it to them except for the parts where Lionheart encounters the Tiger and a few others.<br /><br />The author's words paint vivid pictures of the fantasy world that she is building. She explores the themes of blood sacrifice and good creatures gone evil. Her descriptions of the underworld can be frightening, and there are many characters to begin to keep track of in this one.<br /><br />The unicorn was so deep that I still don't quite understand him.<br /><br />The author is definitely building a fascinating world!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9782738350542938283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/43273641-jane">Jane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314979963" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer525634468995404927">Veiled Rose was such an amazing book—I laughed and cried and cried some more—and I will admit, I wasn't sure if Moonblood could carry on from that. Then I read it. <b>Moonblood is a stunning and vivid sequel that absolutely lives up to every expectation</b> I could've placed upon it.<br/><br/><b>There is so much raw emotion and deep hurt and guilt in this book.</b> It's beautiful and real and just so raw.<br/><br/>Lionheart's struggles were so relatable. <b>I could <i>feel</i> his deep guilt and shame and it really resonated with me.</b> Rose</span>
  <span id="freeText525634468995404927" style="display:none">Veiled Rose was such an amazing book—I laughed and cried and cried some more—and I will admit, I wasn't sure if Moonblood could carry on from that. Then I read it. <b>Moonblood is a stunning and vivid sequel that absolutely lives up to every expectation</b> I could've placed upon it.<br /><br /><b>There is so much raw emotion and deep hurt and guilt in this book.</b> It's beautiful and real and just so raw.<br /><br />Lionheart's struggles were so relatable. <b>I could <i>feel</i> his deep guilt and shame and it really resonated with me.</b> Rose Red's pain and hurt. Oeric, Beana, Felix, Imraldera, Eanrin. <b>All the characters have such real struggles that I became a part of as I read.</b><br /><br />Normally third person doesn't suck me into the story as much as first person. Not so with the Goldstone Wood books. <b>The style of the writing, the deep emotions, and the personality and the core heart behind the story always pulls me in and keeps me turning pages.</b><br /><br /><b>I loved every moment of this story.</b> It didn't make me laugh and cry like Veiled Rose did, but somehow it was still stronger.<br /><br /><b>The finale was so beautiful and so perfect in so many different ways.</b> There was quite a large cast, but Anne handled that expertly and didn't leave anyone out.<br /><br /><b>This book is a beautiful addition to the Goldstone Wood saga</b>, and one of those books leaving me wishing that it had just kept on going with more and more of this vibrant, beautiful story. (Except if it had, I wouldn't have read it, because long books are scary. 😂)</span>

<div id="review_331844728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331844728" />
    <a title="Panda Incognito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4838436-panda-incognito"><img alt="Panda Incognito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301446225p2/4838436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331844728?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Panda Incognito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Panda Incognito" href="/user/show/4838436-panda-incognito">Panda Incognito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838436-panda-incognito?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331844728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9016509157245436323">I thoroughly enjoyed this book! Having already read "Heartless" and "Veiled Rose", I had high expectations for this book, but it still blew me away. With each new release, the author only improves. <br/><br/>I got to meet Anne Elisabeth at a book signing, where I bought my copy of this book. Now, a week later, I've finished the story. Usually, I speed through books that I enjoy, but this time I found myself reading it slowly, savoring the story and beautiful prose.<br/><br/>Remarkably well-crafted, this fantasy ser</span>
  <span id="freeText9016509157245436323" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this book! Having already read "Heartless" and "Veiled Rose", I had high expectations for this book, but it still blew me away. With each new release, the author only improves. <br /><br />I got to meet Anne Elisabeth at a book signing, where I bought my copy of this book. Now, a week later, I've finished the story. Usually, I speed through books that I enjoy, but this time I found myself reading it slowly, savoring the story and beautiful prose.<br /><br />Remarkably well-crafted, this fantasy series stands out among its competitors. This is world which is vivid and believable. Not just a backdrop for the events, this world is fascinating in and of itself, yet even in such a fantastic setting, the characters are still very human.<br /><br />Flawed yet likable, each character is a startlingly accurate portrayal of human nature. In my opinion, Prince Lionheart's story of redemption was the most powerful. <br /><br />I generally can't stand the characters who bumble things up, show poor judgment, and make major mistakes, but I could not bring myself to hate Lionheart. Despite his sin, he wasn't a bad, unfeeling, corrupt person. He was just like you or me. His mistakes were tangled up in a mess of partially good intentions- they did not come from the depths of a wretched heart. He wanted to do the right thing, but his perspective of right was skewed. He wanted to save his people, to save his kingdom. Though he went about it in the wrong way, and the mistakes only snowballed from there, his initial intentions were not as wrong as you might guess when seeing the results of his actions.<br /><br />Yet despite Lionheart's failings, he was not without hope,and neither are we. In a beautiful portrayal of Christ, he is redeemed. The allegory, though tenuous at times, culminates here. It was beautiful to see aspects of the gospel portrayed in this fantasy story, and it moved me in a way that I did not expect. Because Lionheart was so human, so real, so was the story of his redemption.<br /><br />This was a very satisfying series ending. The book tied together the overlapping story threads which carried through the first two novels, turning them into one whole, solid story. I appreciated how we had a chance to see certain events told more than once throughout the books, each time from different a perspective, while still remaining fresh and new. It was wonderful to see how all of the stories fit together in the end, and I cannot wait to read the prequel series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9016509157245436323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_313742519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313742519" />
    <a title="Kathleen (Kat) Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith"><img alt="Kathleen (Kat) Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366143217p2/4328680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313742519?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen (Kat) Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen (Kat) Smith" href="/user/show/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith">Kathleen (Kat) Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=christian-action-adventure">christian-action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=christian-suspense-fiction">christian-suspense-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=christian-fantasy-fiction">christian-fantasy-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=fantasy-adventure-fiction">fantasy-adventure-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=medieval-fantasy-fiction">medieval-fantasy-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=christian-teen-fiction">christian-teen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4328680-kathleen-kat-smith?shelf=science-fiction-and-fantasy">science-fiction-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313742519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1024561578072645157">Moonblood is the third book in Tales of Goldstone Wood series by Anne Elisabeth Stengl. I deeply enjoyed the first two books called Heartless and Veiled Rose where the two main characters are a veiled girl named Rose Red and the Prince of Southlands, Leo or Lionheart as referred to in the book. This story takes place after the dragon that has scorched all of Southlands and several other capitals and countryside's. Leo has come back to sort out many of the problems that have plagued his country f</span>
  <span id="freeText1024561578072645157" style="display:none">Moonblood is the third book in Tales of Goldstone Wood series by Anne Elisabeth Stengl. I deeply enjoyed the first two books called Heartless and Veiled Rose where the two main characters are a veiled girl named Rose Red and the Prince of Southlands, Leo or Lionheart as referred to in the book. This story takes place after the dragon that has scorched all of Southlands and several other capitals and countryside's. Leo has come back to sort out many of the problems that have plagued his country for the 5 long years of imprisonment. The castle and land have been ravaged by the legendary dragon poison where nothing grows and poison seeps into the land and it’s people. Rose Red has promised to stay by Leo’s side, but will that be enough when another dragon is sighted and Rose Red is seen bringing back the limp and unconscious Prince. How will the story end and will this dragon be slayed, or is there some other plot that is unknown!<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this book from beginning to end and loved this series. I would rate this book a 4.5 out of 5 stars for although the content was great, there were times when the chapters would drag out a little and I would find myself falling asleep at night. As for the characters, I simply loved the storyline between Leo, Rose Red, the Price of Farthestshore, Una, Felix the Prince of Parumvir as well as many others. Please pick up the book and read the series from first to last.<br /><br />I received Moonblood by Anne Elisabeth Stengl compliments of Christian Fiction Blog Alliance for my honest review and have to say this has been an incredible series to have the opportunity to read from beginning to end. It's a definite must read for fans of Christian Medieval Fantasy books and the characters, creatures and lands are well-thought out. The best part about Anne's books in this series, is that they are unpredictable in that she doesn't give too much away to the readers at the beginning that they can sense the direction the story is headed. LOVE that in a writer!<br /><br />Now the sad part, I am finished with this book and can only hope that Anne continues to write many more books in the future. Her talent as an author is assured by this reader!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1024561578072645157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_697559165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697559165" />
    <a title="Jenelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4241738-jenelle"><img alt="Jenelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442438882p2/4241738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697559165?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenelle" href="/user/show/4241738-jenelle">Jenelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697559165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4270676015321406698">I’m not sure how to summarize this one without giving away everything, so I’m just going to use the text from the back cover:<br/><br/>In a desperate bid to earn back the trust of his kingdom, Prince Lionheart banishes his only friend, Rose Red, to certain death. Now, his last hope for regaining his honor is to descend into the treacherous Wilderlands and find her.<br/><br/>But many perils stand in Lionheart’s path. A mysterious Hunter is on his trail, a dangerous unicorn prowls the darker shadows, and Rose Red her</span>
  <span id="freeText4270676015321406698" style="display:none">I’m not sure how to summarize this one without giving away everything, so I’m just going to use the text from the back cover:<br /><br />In a desperate bid to earn back the trust of his kingdom, Prince Lionheart banishes his only friend, Rose Red, to certain death. Now, his last hope for regaining his honor is to descend into the treacherous Wilderlands and find her.<br /><br />But many perils stand in Lionheart’s path. A mysterious Hunter is on his trail, a dangerous unicorn prowls the darker shadows, and Rose Red herself has been drawn into the hidden realm of Arpiar where the goblin king holds her captive for foul purposes of his own.<br /><br />With the help of a blind cat, an ugly knight, and the gentle Lady of the Haven, Lionheart can only hope he will find Rose Red before the Night of Moonblood . . . when the sleeping dragons will awake . . . <br /><br />When I finished Veiled Rose, I was very much hoping that Moonblood would pick up where Veiled Rose left off. I felt that Leo’s and Rose Red’s stories simply could NOT end where the previous book had left them. There had to be more. However, I was not sure what to expect, since the author had already switched characters on me between Heartless and Veiled Rose. I was not quite ready to embrace yet another new character-cast.<br /><br />Thankfully, Moonblood does, in fact, pick up pretty much where Veiled Rose ends – and helps tie together more of the characters from both of the previous books. So, while we still mostly follow Leo and Rose Red, we also get reintroduced to Felix. I also enjoyed getting to know more about Eanrin, as he is a far more prominent figure in this book than in the first two.<br /><br />I think that perhaps this has been my favorite of this series so far… though the tiny bit of relationship left unresolved at the ending does make me desperately hope for more stories with the characters Leo, Felix, and Rose Red (as the next set of books starts up 1600 years before the beginning of “Heartless”).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4270676015321406698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_341408272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341408272" />
    <a title="Shauna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5052230-shauna"><img alt="Shauna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338936552p2/5052230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341408272?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shauna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shauna" href="/user/show/5052230-shauna">Shauna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341408272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3593618463654785244">Get some business out of the way first of all. I received a free copy of this book from Bethany House Publishers for review and am not paid for this review. If you would like to review your own copies please contact <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bethanyhouse.com/bookreviewers'>www.bethanyhouse.com/bookreviewers</a>.<br/><br/> <br/><br/>Now on with the review... The first thing that struck me about this book was the title. I just bugs me and makes me think of something with a completely different meaning if you get my drift. I think there could have been some better alternatives. </span>
  <span id="freeText3593618463654785244" style="display:none">Get some business out of the way first of all. I received a free copy of this book from Bethany House Publishers for review and am not paid for this review. If you would like to review your own copies please contact <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bethanyhouse.com/bookreviewers">www.bethanyhouse.com/bookreviewers</a>.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Now on with the review... The first thing that struck me about this book was the title. I just bugs me and makes me think of something with a completely different meaning if you get my drift. I think there could have been some better alternatives. As I started reading the book, some of the character names struck me as a little childish... Rose Red, Prince Lionheart....<br /><br /><br />However, once I got over my annoyance at these little things, I found the story to be so enjoyable. I did not know there were a couple books prior to this one and reading those would help fill in some of the backstory but not a big deal. The characters were very real, dealing with emotions we all feel and could relate to in some way. I also didn't like seeing a unicorn turned into a bad creature for this story, but I guess we all can fall from grace, even something as innocent as a unicorn.<br /><br /><br />The book is full of Christian allegories with the Prince as a Christ-like figure and grace and forgiveness for all the faults of the characters. That's all fine and dandy to me, but I don't read to find symbolism or hidden meanings and had I not known prior to reading it, I probably never would have picked up on it. Takes too much effort for me to dissect a story. I read it and enjoy it in the moment. If something hits me later, great. If not, I don't feel I missed out on anything.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Overall it was far better than I expected when I first started reading it. I really enjoyed it and plan on someday reading the previous two books and whatever may come after. Fun, middle grade fantasy.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Hope you enjoy it too! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3593618463654785244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1530467984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530467984" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33279488-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555812564p2/33279488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1530467984?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/33279488-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18214156-moonblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33279488-gabrielle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33279488-gabrielle?shelf=allegory">allegory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530467984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer698978033477136076"><strong>Enchanting-in more ways than one</strong><br/><br/>This book was wonderful. I must admit, after reading the second book in the series, Veiled Rose, I was a little disappointed. Especially following such a book as Heartless. But Moonblood helped me fall in love with the series all over again.<br/>If you haven't read the first two, you need to go do that. Like, RIGHT NOW. The first one is the best, but you also need to read the second one to really get an understanding of what's going on in this one.<br/>My favorite parts of </span>
  <span id="freeText698978033477136076" style="display:none"><strong>Enchanting-in more ways than one</strong><br /><br />This book was wonderful. I must admit, after reading the second book in the series, Veiled Rose, I was a little disappointed. Especially following such a book as Heartless. But Moonblood helped me fall in love with the series all over again.<br />If you haven't read the first two, you need to go do that. Like, RIGHT NOW. The first one is the best, but you also need to read the second one to really get an understanding of what's going on in this one.<br />My favorite parts of this one were Arpiar (what an amazing place-I can almost smell the roses), Sir Eanrin (who doesn't like the sarcastic cat/knight?), and *Major Spoilers* -no seriously-if you plan on reading any of the first three books and haven't yet, skip the spoiler section. I warned you!-how Lionheart came back to life and Varvare got to be actually beautiful in the end. Even though I didn't care for Lionheart much, I would have been disappointed had the author actually let him be dead. And I had always hoped that Rosie would eventually become beautiful. ;) *End of Spoilers*<br />This book was a little bit darker and more violent than the first two, (which are pretty dark and violent in themselves), but you really don't want to miss this one. It has such great themes about self-sacrifice, finding forgiveness while knowing there is nothing you can do to earn it, and repentance. I found myself highlighting and sharing many great passages, especially towards the end, and my eyes even grew a little misty at certain parts. Truly a wonderful third book in the Tales of Goldstone Woods series. On to the next one!<br /><br />Rating:5 Stars<br /><br />Violence/Graphic: 7/10<br />Sexual Content: 0/10<br />Language: 1/10 (made up phrases such as 'hen's teeth' and 'iubdan's beard')<br /><br />Recommendation: Most definitely recommended. 14 and up, with a warning for sensitive readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="698978033477136076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gK6tV60Tv37yycz98mSaXPvhLdWkktxfcGmcv/mOe6R2FDpaF5YMHK/tYSfobO4HNNmTD3ezmWTaFPrBSCR/Jw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jjR+l0peyOVIyZau8c1RPwj4HexPmwYDvvfcJCWcxCl4juma8Nt7hxXtO3TrxSVkx8CjNpy6QzgUirpalDbAqg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer12402771986361483228">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking.   <span id="freeText12402771986361483228" style="display:none">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking. She studied illustration at Grace College and English literature at Campbell University. She is the author of the TALES OF GOLDSTONE WOOD, which currently includes seven novels and two novellas, with plenty more works due to release over the next few years. Her novels HEARTLESS, VEILED ROSE, and DRAGONWITCH have each been honored with a Christy Award, and STARFLOWER was voted winner of the 2013 Clive Staples Award.</span>
